<th style="padding-right:1em">Date</th>
<td>April 25, 1846 – February 3, 1848<br/>
(1 year, 9 months, 1 week and 1 day)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Location</th>
<td><span class="location">Texas, New Mexico, California; Northern, Central, and Eastern Mexico; Mexico City</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding-right:1em">Result</th>
<td>
<p>American victory</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a></li>
<li>Mexican recognition of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> (among other territories) as independent; End of <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">conflict</a> between Mexico and Texas</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Mexico" title="Template:History of Mexico"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Mexico" title="Template talk:History of Mexico"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Mexico&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Mexican–American War</b>, also known as the <b>Mexican War</b>, the <b>U.S.–Mexican War</b> or the <b>Invasion of Mexico</b>, was an armed conflict between the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">United Mexican States</a> from 1846 to 1848. It followed in the wake of the 1845 US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Annexation" title="Texas Annexation">annexation of Texas</a>, which Mexico considered part of its territory, despite the 1836 <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">Texas Revolution</a>.</p>
<p>After its <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Treaty of Córdoba">independence in 1821</a> and brief experiment with monarchy, Mexico became a republic in 1824. It was characterized by considerable instability, so that when war broke out in 1846, Mexico was ill-prepared for conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The war with the United States followed in the wake of decades of <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> raids in the sparsely settled north of Mexico, which prompted the Mexican government to sponsor migration from the US to the Mexican province of Texas to act as a buffer. Texans from both countries revolted against the Mexican government in the 1836 Texas Revolution, creating a republic not recognized by Mexico, which still claimed it as its national territory. The 1845 expansion of US territory with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Annexation" title="Texas Annexation">annexation of Texas</a> escalated the dispute between the United States and Mexico to open war.</p>
<p>In 1844, <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a>, the newly-elected US president, made a proposition to the Mexican government to purchase the disputed lands between the <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">Nueces River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>. When that offer was rejected, troops from the United States commanded by Major General <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">Zachary Taylor</a> were moved into the disputed territory of Coahuila. These troops were then <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Affair" title="Thornton Affair">attacked</a> by Mexican troops, killing 12 US troops and taking 52 prisoners. These same Mexican troops later laid siege to a US fort along the Rio Grande.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> This would lead to the conflict that resulted in the loss of much of Mexico's northern territory.</p>
<p>US forces quickly occupied <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Santa Fe de Nuevo México</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alta_California_Territory" title="Alta California Territory">Alta California Territory</a>, and then invaded parts of Central Mexico (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_Mexico" title="Northeastern Mexico">Northeastern Mexico</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Mexico" title="Northwest Mexico">Northwest Mexico</a>); meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Squadron" title="Pacific Squadron">Pacific Squadron</a> conducted a blockade, and took control of several garrisons on the Pacific coast farther south in <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Territory" title="Baja California Territory">Baja California Territory</a>. The US army, under the command of Major General <a href="/wiki/Winfield_Scott" title="Winfield Scott">Winfield Scott</a>, captured the capital <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, marching from the port of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>.</p>
<p>The 1848 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a> ended and specified the major consequence of the war: the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">Mexican Cession</a> of the territories of Alta California and Santa Fe de Nuevo México to the United States. The US agreed to pay $15 million compensation for the physical damage of war. In addition, the United States assumed $3.25 million of debt owed by the Mexican government to US citizens. Mexico acknowledged the loss of Texas and thereafter cited the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> as its national border with the United States.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territorial_expansion_of_the_United_States" title="Territorial expansion of the United States">territorial expansion of the United States</a> toward the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_coast_of_the_United_States" title="Pacific coast of the United States">Pacific coast</a> had been the goal of US President <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> At first, the war was highly controversial in the United States, with the <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig Party</a>, anti-imperialists, and anti-slavery elements strongly opposed. Critics in the United States pointed to the heavy casualties of US forces and the high monetary cost of the conflict. The war intensified the issue of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">slavery in the United States</a>, leading to bitter debates that culminated in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. However, even the most bitter opponents of the war expressed their delight at the enormous spoils won by the United States.</p>
<p>In Mexico, the war came in the middle of political turmoil, which increased into chaos during the conflict. The military defeat and loss of territory was a disastrous blow, causing Mexico to enter "a period of self-examination ... as its leaders sought to identify and address the reasons that had led to such a debacle."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In the immediate aftermath of the war, some prominent Mexicans wrote that the war had resulted in "the state of degradation and ruin" in Mexico, further claiming, for "the true origin of the war, it is sufficient to say that the insatiable ambition of the United States, favored by our weakness, caused it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The shift in the Mexico-U.S. border left many Mexican citizens separated from their national government. For the indigenous peoples who had never accepted Mexican rule, the change in border meant conflicts with a new outside power.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roots_of_the_conflict_in_Northern_Mexico">Roots of the conflict in Northern Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Roots of the conflict in Northern Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comanches.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Comanches.jpg/220px-Comanches.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Comanches.jpg/330px-Comanches.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Comanches.jpg/440px-Comanches.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Comanches.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Comanches of West <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> in war regalia, c. 1830.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_1832,_Region_Comanche.PNG"><img alt="An Osage The boundaries of Comancheria -- the Comanche homeland." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="885" data-file-width="885" height="400" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG/400px-Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG/600px-Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG/800px-Mexico_1832%2C_Region_Comanche.PNG 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_1832,_Region_Comanche.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 1832 boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Comancheria" title="Comancheria">Comancheria</a>, the Comanche homeland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The northern area of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> was sparsely settled and not well controlled politically by the government based in Mexico City. After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_independence" title="Mexican independence">independence</a> from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in 1821, Mexico contended with internal struggles that sometimes verged on civil war. In the sparsely settled interior of northern Mexico, the end of Spanish colonial rule was marked by the end of financing for <a href="/wiki/Presidio" title="Presidio">presidios</a> and for subsidies to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_Americans" title="Indigenous Americans">indigenous Americans</a> to maintain the peace. There were conflicts between indigenous people in the northern region as well. The <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">Comanche</a> were particularly successful in expanding their territory in the <a href="/wiki/Comanche%E2%80%93Mexico_Wars" title="Comanche–Mexico Wars">Comanche–Mexico Wars</a> and garnering resources. The <a href="/wiki/Apache%E2%80%93Mexico_Wars" title="Apache–Mexico Wars">Apache–Mexico Wars</a> also made Mexico's north a violent place, with no effective political control.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Apache" title="Apache">Apache</a> raids left thousands of people dead through out northern Mexico. When the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> entered northern Mexico in 1846 they found a demoralized people. There was little resistance to US forces from the civilian population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hostile activity from indigenous people also made communications and trade between the interior of Mexico and provinces such as <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">New Mexico</a> difficult. As a result, New Mexico was dependent on the overland <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Trail" title="Santa Fe Trail">Santa Fe Trail</a> trade with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> at the outbreak of the Mexican–American War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The military and diplomatic capabilities of Mexico declined after it attained independence and left the northern half of the country vulnerable to the Comanche, Apache, and <a href="/wiki/Navajo" title="Navajo">Navajo</a>. The indigenous people, especially the Comanche, took advantage of the weakness of the Mexican state to undertake large-scale raids hundreds of miles into the country to acquire livestock for their own use and to supply an expanding market in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mexican government's policy of settlement of US citizens in its province of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Texas" title="Mexican Texas">Tejas</a> was aimed at expanding control into Comanche lands, the <a href="/wiki/Comancheria" title="Comancheria">Comancheria</a>. Instead of settlement occurring in the central and west of the province, people settled in <a href="/wiki/East_Texas" title="East Texas">East Texas</a>, where there was rich farmland and which was contiguous to southern US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_state" title="Slave state">slave states</a>. As settlers poured in from the US, the Mexican government took steps to discourage further settlement, including its 1829 abolition of slavery.</p>
<p>In 1836 Mexico was relatively united in refusing to recognize the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">independence of Texas</a>. Mexico threatened war with the United States if it annexed the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Meanwhile, U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_Polk" title="President Polk">President Polk</a>'s assertion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manifest_Destiny" title="Manifest Destiny">Manifest Destiny</a> was focusing United States interest on westward expansion beyond its existing national borders.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Designs_on_California">Designs on California</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Designs on California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the Spanish colonial era, the Californias (i.e., the Baja California peninsula and Alta California) were sparsely settled. After Mexico became independent, it shut down the missions and reduced its military presence.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_1824_(equirectangular_projection).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1047" data-file-width="1400" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png/250px-Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png/375px-Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png/500px-Mexico_1824_%28equirectangular_projection%29.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_1824_(equirectangular_projection).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Republic" title="First Mexican Republic">Mexico</a> in 1824. <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> is the northwestern-most state.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1842, the US minister in Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Waddy_Thompson,_Jr." title="Waddy Thompson, Jr.">Waddy Thompson, Jr.</a>, suggested Mexico might be willing to cede Alta California to settle debts, saying: "As to Texas, I regard it as of very little value compared with California, the richest, the most beautiful, and the healthiest country in the world ... with the acquisition of Upper California we should have the same ascendency on the Pacific ... France and England both have had their eyes upon it."</p>
<p>US President <a href="/wiki/John_Tyler" title="John Tyler">John Tyler</a>'s administration suggested a tripartite pact that would settle the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_boundary_dispute" title="Oregon boundary dispute">Oregon boundary dispute</a> and provide for the cession of the port of San Francisco from Mexico; <a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton-Gordon,_4th_Earl_of_Aberdeen" title="George Hamilton-Gordon, 4th Earl of Aberdeen">Lord Aberdeen</a> declined to participate but said Britain had no objection to U.S. territorial acquisition there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British minister in Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pakenham" title="Richard Pakenham">Richard Pakenham</a>, wrote in 1841 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Palmerston" title="Lord Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a> urging "to establish an English population in the magnificent Territory of Upper California", saying that "no part of the World offering greater natural advantages for the establishment of an English colony ... by all means desirable ... that California, once ceasing to belong to Mexico, should not fall into the hands of any power but England ... daring and adventurous speculators in the United States have already turned their thoughts in this direction." But by the time the letter reached London, Sir <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peel" title="Robert Peel">Robert Peel</a>'s Tory government, with its <a href="/wiki/Little_Englander" title="Little Englander">Little England</a> policy, had come to power and rejected the proposal as expensive and a potential source of conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>A significant number of influential <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">Californios</a> were in favor of annexation, either by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> or by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>. <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_Pico" title="Pío Pico">Pío de Jesús Pico IV</a>, the last governor of Alta California, was in favor of British annexation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Texas">Republic of Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Republic of Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_annexation" title="Texas annexation">Texas annexation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Texas_Revolution" title="Texas Revolution">Texas Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="410" data-file-width="333" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/220px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/330px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg/440px-Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wpdms_republic_of_texas.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>. The present-day outlines of the individual US states are superimposed on the boundaries of 1836–1845.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1800, the colonial province of Texas was sparsely populated, with only about 7,000 non-Indian settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Santoni_1511_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Santoni_1511-20">[20]</a></sup> The Spanish crown developed a policy of colonization to more effectively control the territory. After independence, the Mexican government implemented the policy, granting <a href="/wiki/Moses_Austin" title="Moses Austin">Moses Austin</a>, a banker from Missouri, a large tract of land in Texas. Austin died before he could bring his plan of recruiting American settlers for the land to fruition, but his son, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_F._Austin" title="Stephen F. Austin">Stephen F. Austin</a>, brought over 300 American families into Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> This started the steady trend of migration from the United States into the Texas frontier. Austin's colony was the most successful of several colonies authorized by the Mexican government. The Mexican government intended the new settlers to act as a buffer between the <a href="/wiki/Tejano" title="Tejano">Tejano</a> residents and the <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">Comanches</a>, but the non-Hispanic colonists tended to settle where there was decent farmland and trade connections with American Louisiana, which the United States had acquired in the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>, rather than further west where they would have been an effective buffer against the Indians.</p>
<p>In 1829, as a result of the large influx of American immigrants, the non-Hispanic outnumbered native Spanish speakers in the Texas territory. President <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Guerrero" title="Vicente Guerrero">Vicente Guerrero</a>, a hero of Mexican independence, moved to gain more control over Texas and its influx of southern non-Hispanic colonists and discourage further immigration by abolishing slavery in Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Santoni_1511_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Santoni_1511-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Mexican government also decided to reinstate the property tax and increase tariffs on shipped American goods. The settlers and many Mexican businessmen in the region rejected the demands, which led to Mexico closing Texas to additional immigration, which continued from the United States into Texas illegally.</p>
<p>In 1834, General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> became the centralist dictator of Mexico, abandoning the federal system. He decided to quash the semi-independence of Texas, having succeeded in doing so in Coahuila (in 1824, Mexico had merged Texas and Coahuila into the massive state of <a href="/wiki/Coahuila_y_Tejas" title="Coahuila y Tejas">Coahuila y Tejas</a>). Finally, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_F._Austin" title="Stephen F. Austin">Stephen F. Austin</a> called Texians to arms; they declared independence from Mexico in 1836, and after Santa Anna <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Alamo" title="Battle of the Alamo">defeated the Texians at the Alamo</a>, he was defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Texian_Army" title="Texian Army">Texian Army</a> commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston" title="Sam Houston">Sam Houston</a> and captured at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Jacinto" title="Battle of San Jacinto">Battle of San Jacinto</a> and signed a treaty recognizing Texas' independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Republic_of_Texas_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_Texas-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Texas consolidated its status as an independent republic and received official recognition from Britain, France, and the United States, which all advised Mexico not to try to reconquer the new nation. Most <a href="/wiki/Texians" title="Texians">Texians</a> wanted to join the United States of America, but annexation of Texas was contentious in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">US Congress</a>, where Whigs were largely opposed. In 1845 Texas agreed to the offer of annexation by the US Congress. Texas became the 28th state on December 29, 1845.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Republic_of_Texas_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Republic_of_Texas-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_of_the_war">Origins of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origins of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The border of Texas as an independent state was originally never settled. The Republic of Texas claimed land up to the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Velasco" title="Treaties of Velasco">Treaties of Velasco</a>, but Mexico refused to accept these as valid, claiming that the Rio Grande in the treaty was the Nueces, and referred to the Rio Grande as the Rio Bravo. The ill-fated <a href="/wiki/Texan_Santa_Fe_Expedition" title="Texan Santa Fe Expedition">Texan Santa Fe Expedition</a> of 1841 attempted to realize the claim to New Mexican territory East of the Rio Grande, but its members were captured and imprisoned.</p>
<p>Reference to the Rio Grande boundary of Texas was omitted from the US Congress's annexation resolution to help secure passage after the annexation treaty failed in the Senate. President Polk claimed the Rio Grande boundary, and when Mexico sent forces over the Rio Grande, this provoked a dispute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 1845, Polk sent General <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">Zachary Taylor</a> to Texas, and by October 3,500 Americans were on the <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">Nueces River</a>, ready to take by force the disputed land. Polk wanted to protect the border and also coveted for the U.S. the continent clear to the Pacific Ocean. At the same time Polk wrote to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Larkin" title="Thomas O. Larkin">Thomas Larkin</a>, the American consul in the Mexican territory of Alta California, disclaiming American ambitions in California, but offering to support independence from Mexico or voluntary accession to the United States, and warning that the United States would oppose a British or French takeover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rives.2C_vol._2.2C_pp._165.E2.80.93168-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>To end another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fifty-Four_Forty_or_Fight" title="Fifty-Four Forty or Fight">war scare with the United Kingdom</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">Oregon Country</a>, Polk signed the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Treaty" title="Oregon Treaty">Oregon Treaty</a> dividing the territory, angering northern Democrats who felt he was prioritizing Southern expansion over Northern expansion.</p>
<p>In the Winter of 1845–46, the federally commissioned explorer <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frémont">John C. Frémont</a> and a group of armed men appeared in Alta California. After telling the Mexican governor and the American Consul Larkin he was merely buying supplies on the way to Oregon, he instead went to the populated area of California and visited <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_County,_California" title="Santa Cruz County, California">Santa Cruz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salinas_Valley" title="Salinas Valley">Salinas Valley</a>, explaining he had been looking for a seaside home for his mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Mexican authorities became alarmed and ordered him to leave. Frémont responded by building a fort on <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Peak_(California)" title="Fremont Peak (California)">Gavilan Peak</a> and raising the American flag. Larkin sent word that Frémont's actions were counterproductive. Frémont left California in March but returned to California and took control of the <a href="/wiki/California_Battalion" title="California Battalion">California Battalion</a> following the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/California_Republic#Bear_Flag_Revolt" title="California Republic">Bear Flag Revolt</a> in Sonoma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November, 1845, Polk sent <a href="/wiki/John_Slidell" title="John Slidell">John Slidell</a>, a secret representative, to Mexico City with an offer to the Mexican government of $25 million for the Rio Grande border in Texas and Mexico's provinces of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Santa Fe de Nuevo México</a>. US expansionists wanted California to thwart British ambitions in the area and to gain a port on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. Polk authorized Slidell to forgive the $3 million owed to US citizens for damages caused by the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a> and pay another $25 to $30 million in exchange for the two territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mexico was not inclined nor able to negotiate. In 1846 alone, the presidency changed hands four times, the war ministry six times, and the finance ministry sixteen times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Mexican public opinion and all political factions agreed that selling the territories to the United States would tarnish the national honor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Mexicans who opposed direct conflict with the United States, including President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Herrera" title="José Joaquín de Herrera">José Joaquín de Herrera</a>, were viewed as traitors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks6162_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks6162-31">[31]</a></sup> Military opponents of de Herrera, supported by populist newspapers, considered Slidell's presence in Mexico City an insult. When de Herrera considered receiving Slidell to settle the problem of Texas annexation peacefully, he was accused of treason and deposed. After a more nationalistic government under General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mariano_Paredes_y_Arrillaga" title="Mariano Paredes y Arrillaga">Mariano Paredes y Arrillaga</a> came to power, it publicly reaffirmed Mexico's claim to Texas;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks6162_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks6162-31">[31]</a></sup> Slidell, convinced that Mexico should be "chastised", returned to the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparation_for_war">Preparation for war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Preparation for war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenges_in_Mexico">Challenges in Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Challenges in Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican_Army">Mexican Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mexican Army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="480" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG/220px-Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG/330px-Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG/440px-Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oleo_Antonio_Lopez_de_Santa_Anna.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> was a military hero who became president of Mexico on multiple occasions. The Mexican Army's intervention in politics was an ongoing issue during much of the mid-nineteenth century.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mexican Army emerged from the war of independence (1810-1821) as a weak and divided force. Before the war with the United States, the military faced both internal and foreign challenges. The Spanish still occupied the coastal fortress of San Juan de Ulúa, and Spain did not recognize Mexico's independence, so that the new nation was at risk for invasion. In 1829, the Spanish attempted to reconquer their former colony and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> became a national hero defending the homeland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The army had a set of privileges (<i>fueros</i>), established in the colonial era, that gave it jurisdiction over many aspects of its affairs. In general, the military supported conservative positions, advocating a strong central government and upholding privileges of the military and the Catholic Church.</p>
<p>Some military men exercised power in local areas as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caudillos" title="Caudillos">caudillos</a> and resisted central command. Liberal politicians, such as <a href="/wiki/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas" title="Valentín Gómez Farías">Valentín Gómez Farías</a>, sought to rein in the military's power. The military faced insurrections and separatist movements in Tabasco, Yucatán, and Texas. The French blockaded in Veracruz in 1838 to collect debts, a conflict known to history as the <a href="/wiki/Pastry_War" title="Pastry War">Pastry War</a>. Compounding the demands on the Mexican military, there were continuing Indian challenges to power in the northern region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the Mexican side, only 7 of the 19 states that formed the Mexican federation sent soldiers, armament, and money for the war effort, as the young Republic had not yet developed a sense of a unifying, national identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mexican soldiers were not easily melded into an effective fighting force. Santa Anna said "the leaders of the army did their best to train the rough men who volunteered, but they could do little to inspire them with patriotism for the glorious country they were honored to serve."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> According to leading conservative politician <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Alam%C3%A1n" title="Lucas Alamán">Lucas Alamán</a>, the "money spent on arming Mexican troops merely enabled them to fight each other and 'give the illusion' that the country possessed an army for its defense."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> However, an officer criticized Santa Anna's training of troops, "The cavalry was drilled only in regiments. The artillery hardly ever maneuvered and never fired a blank shot. The general in command was never present on the field of maneuvers, so that he was unable to appreciate the respective qualities of the various bodies under his command.... If any meetings of the principal commanding officers were held to discuss the operations of the campaign, it was not known, nor was it known whether any plan of campaign had been formed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the war, Mexican forces were divided between the permanent forces (<i>permanentes</i>) and the active militiamen (<i>activos</i>). The permanent forces consisted of 12 regiments of infantry (of two battalions each), three brigades of artillery, eight regiments of cavalry, one separate squadron and a brigade of dragoons. The militia amounted to nine infantry and six cavalry regiments. In the northern territories of Mexico, presidial companies (<i>presidiales</i>) protected the scattered settlements there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the contributing factors to loss of the war by Mexico was the inferiority of their weapons. The Mexican army was using surplus British <a href="/wiki/Musket" title="Musket">muskets</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Brown_Bess" title="Brown Bess">Brown Bess</a>) from the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> period. While at the beginning of the war the majority of American soldiers were still equipped with the very similar Springfield 1816 flintlock muskets, more reliable <a href="/wiki/Caplock_mechanism" title="Caplock mechanism">caplock</a> models gained large inroads within the rank and file as the conflict progressed. Some US troops carried radically modern weapons that gave them a significant advantage over their Mexican counterparts, such as the Springfield 1841 rifle of the Mississippi Rifles and the Colt Paterson revolver of the Texas Rangers. In the later stages of the war, the US Mounted Rifles were issued <a href="/wiki/Colt_Walker" title="Colt Walker">Colt Walker</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolvers" title="Revolvers">revolvers</a>, of which the US Army had ordered 1,000 in 1846. Most significantly, throughout the war the superiority of the US artillery often carried the day. While technologically Mexican and American artillery operated on the same plane, US army training as well as the quality and reliability of their logistics gave US guns and cannoneers a significant edge.</p>
<p>Desertion was a major problem for the Mexican army, depleting forces on the eve of battle. Most soldiers were peasants who had a loyalty to their village and family, but not to the generals who had conscripted them. Often hungry and ill, under-equipped, only partially trained, and never well paid, the soldiers were held in contempt by their officers and had little reason to fight the invading US forces. Looking for their opportunity, many slipped away from camp to find their way back to their home village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_divisions">Political divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Political divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas,_portrait.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="425" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas%2C_portrait.JPG/220px-Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas%2C_portrait.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas%2C_portrait.JPG/330px-Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas%2C_portrait.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas%2C_portrait.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas,_portrait.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Liberal <a href="/wiki/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas" title="Valentín Gómez Farías">Valentín Gómez Farías</a>, who served as Santa Anna's vice president and implemented a liberal reform in 1833, was an important political player in the era of the Mexican–American War.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Political divisions inside Mexico were another factor in the US victory. Inside Mexico, the <i>centralistas</i> and <i>republicanos</i> vied for power, and at times these two factions inside Mexico's military fought each other rather than the invading US Army. Another faction called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monarchists" title="Monarchists">monarchists</a>, whose members wanted to install a <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a> (some advocated rejoining Spain), further complicated matters. This third faction would rise to predominance in the period of the <a href="/wiki/French_intervention_in_Mexico" title="French intervention in Mexico">French intervention in Mexico</a>. The ease of the American landing at <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> was in large part due to civil warfare in Mexico City, which made any real defense of the port city impossible. As Gen. Santa Anna said, "However shameful it may be to admit this, we have brought this disgraceful tragedy upon ourselves through our interminable in-fighting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Army">United States Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United States Army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._Army,_Navy,_and_volunteer_units_in_the_Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="List of U.S. Army, Navy, and volunteer units in the Mexican–American War">List of U.S. Army, Navy, and volunteer units in the Mexican–American War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_nebel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="640" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/250px-Mexico_nebel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/375px-Mexico_nebel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Mexico_nebel.jpg/500px-Mexico_nebel.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_nebel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. Army occupation of <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> in 1847. The American flag is flying over the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a>, the seat of the Mexican government.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the American side, the war was fought by regiments of regulars and various regiments, battalions, and companies of volunteers from the different states of the Union and the Americans and some of the Mexicans in the territory of California and New Mexico. On the West Coast, the US Navy fielded a battalion of sailors, in an attempt to recapture <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Although the US Army and Navy were not large at the outbreak of the war, the officers were generally well trained and the numbers of enlisted men fairly large compared to Mexico's. At the beginning of the war, the US Army had eight regiments of infantry (three battalions each), four artillery regiments and three mounted regiments (two dragoons, one of mounted rifles). These regiments were supplemented by 10 new regiments (nine of infantry and one of cavalry) raised for one year of service by the act of Congress from February 11, 1847.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>State volunteers were raised in various sized units and for various periods of time, mostly for one year. Later some were raised for the duration of the war as it became clear it was going to last longer than a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>US soldiers' memoirs describe cases of looting and murder of Mexican civilians, mostly by State Volunteers. One officer's diary records:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We reached Burrita about 5 pm, many of the Louisiana volunteers were there, a lawless drunken rabble. They had driven away the inhabitants, taken possession of their houses, and were emulating each other in making beasts of themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_L._O%27Sullivan" title="John L. O'Sullivan">John L. O'Sullivan</a>, a vocal proponent of Manifest Destiny, later recalled:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The regulars regarded the volunteers with importance and contempt ... [The volunteers] robbed Mexicans of their cattle and corn, stole their fences for firewood, got drunk, and killed several inoffensive inhabitants of the town in the streets.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Many of the volunteers were unwanted and considered poor soldiers. The expression "Just like Gaines's army" came to refer to something useless, the phrase having originated when a group of untrained and unwilling Louisiana troops were rejected and sent back by Gen. Taylor at the Kachow beginning of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>1,563 US soldiers are buried in the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_National_Cemetery" title="Mexico City National Cemetery">Mexico City National Cemetery</a>, which is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/American_Battle_Monuments_Commission" title="American Battle Monuments Commission">American Battle Monuments Commission</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outbreak_of_the_war">Outbreak of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Outbreak of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_skirmish_at_the_Nueces_Strip">Initial skirmish at the Nueces Strip</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Initial skirmish at the Nueces Strip">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nueces_Strip" title="Nueces Strip">Nueces Strip</a></div>
<p>President James K. Polk ordered General Taylor and his forces south to the Rio Grande, entering the territory that Mexicans disputed. Mexico laid claim to all the lands as far north as the <a href="/wiki/Nueces_River" title="Nueces River">Nueces River</a>—about 150 mi (240 km) north of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>. The U.S. claimed that the border was the Rio Grande, citing the 1836 <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Velasco" title="Treaties of Velasco">Treaties of Velasco</a>. However, Mexico rejected the treaties and refused to negotiate, instead still claiming all of Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Taylor ignored Mexican demands to withdraw to the Nueces. He constructed a makeshift fort (later known as <a href="/wiki/Fort_Brown" title="Fort Brown">Fort Brown/Fort Texas</a>) on the banks of the Rio Grande opposite the city of <a href="/wiki/Matamoros,_Tamaulipas" title="Matamoros, Tamaulipas">Matamoros, Tamaulipas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mexican forces under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Santa_Anna" title="General Santa Anna">General Santa Anna</a> immediately prepared for war. On April 25, 1846, a 2,000-man Mexican cavalry detachment attacked a 70-man U.S. patrol under the command of Captain Seth Thornton, which had been sent into the contested territory north of the Rio Grande and south of the Nueces River. In the <a href="/wiki/Thornton_Affair" title="Thornton Affair">Thornton Affair</a>, the Mexican cavalry routed the patrol, killing 11 American soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Regarding the beginning of the war, <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a>, who had opposed the war but served as an army lieutenant in Taylor's Army, claims in his "Personal Memoirs" (1885) that the main goal of the U.S. Army's advance from Nueces River to Rio Grande was to provoke the outbreak of war without attacking first, to debilitate any political opposition to the war.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>The presence of United States troops on the edge of the disputed territory farthest from the Mexican settlements, was not sufficient to provoke hostilities. We were sent to provoke a fight, but it was essential that Mexico should commence it. It was very doubtful whether Congress would declare war; but if Mexico should attack our troops, the Executive could announce, "Whereas, war exists by the acts of, etc.," and prosecute the contest with vigor. Once initiated there were but few public men who would have the courage to oppose it....</p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<p>Mexico showing no willingness to come to the Nueces to drive the invaders from her soil, it became necessary for the "invaders" to approach to within a convenient distance to be struck. Accordingly, preparations were begun for moving the army to the Rio Grande, to a point near Matamoras (sic). It was desirable to occupy a position near the largest centre of population possible to reach, without absolutely invading territory to which we set up no claim whatever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_hostilities">Further hostilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Further hostilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Remember_Your_Regiment,_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series,_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2740" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/230px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/345px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg/460px-Remember_Your_Regiment%2C_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series%2C_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Remember_Your_Regiment,_U.S._Army_in_Action_Series,_2d_Dragoons_charge_in_Mexican_War_1846.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Captain <a href="/wiki/Charles_A._May" title="Charles A. May">Charles A. May</a>'s squadron of the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="2nd Cavalry Regiment (United States)">2nd Dragoons</a> slashes through the Mexican Army lines. <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">Resaca de la Palma</a>, Texas, May 9, 1846</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A few days after the defeat of the U.S. troops by General Arista, the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Texas" title="Siege of Fort Texas">Siege of Fort Texas</a> began on May 3, 1846. Mexican artillery at Matamoros opened fire on Fort Texas, which replied with its own guns. The bombardment continued for 160 hours<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-52">[52]</a></sup> and expanded as Mexican forces gradually surrounded the fort. Thirteen U.S. soldiers were injured during the bombardment, and two were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-52">[52]</a></sup> Among the dead was Jacob Brown, after whom the fort was later named.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 8, Zachary Taylor and 2,400 troops arrived to relieve the fort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> However, General Arista rushed north and intercepted him with a force of 3,400 at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Alto" title="Battle of Palo Alto">Palo Alto</a>. The U.S. Army employed "flying artillery", their term for <a href="/wiki/Horse_artillery" title="Horse artillery">horse artillery</a>, a type of mobile light artillery that was mounted on horse carriages with the entire crew riding horses into battle. It had a devastating effect on the Mexican army. In contrast to the "flying artillery" of the Americans, the Mexican cannons at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palo_Alto" title="Battle of Palo Alto">Battle of Palo Alto</a> fired at such slow velocities that it was possible for American soldiers to dodge artillery rounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The Mexicans replied with cavalry skirmishes and their own artillery. The U.S. flying artillery somewhat demoralized the Mexican side, and seeking terrain more to their advantage, the Mexicans retreated to the far side of a dry riverbed <i>(<a href="/wiki/Resaca_(channel)" title="Resaca (channel)">resaca</a>)</i> during the night. It provided a natural fortification, but during the retreat, Mexican troops were scattered, making communication difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Resaca_de_la_Palma" title="Battle of Resaca de la Palma">Battle of Resaca de la Palma</a> the next day, the two sides engaged in fierce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand_to_hand_combat" title="Hand to hand combat">hand to hand combat</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cavalry" title="United States Cavalry">U.S. Cavalry</a> managed to capture the Mexican artillery, causing the Mexican side to retreat—a retreat that turned into a rout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brooks122_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-Brooks122-52">[52]</a></sup> Fighting on unfamiliar terrain, his troops fleeing in retreat, Arista found it impossible to rally his forces. Mexican casualties were heavy, and the Mexicans were forced to abandon their artillery and baggage. Fort Brown inflicted additional casualties as the withdrawing troops passed by the fort. Many Mexican soldiers drowned trying to swim across the Rio Grande.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Both these engagements were fought before war was declared.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Declarations_of_war">Declarations of war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Declarations of war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div aria-labelledby="Texas_Campaign" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">

<td style="width:25%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FEE8B1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Disputed territory</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EFE0C7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> United States territory, 1848</div>
</td>
<td style="width:25%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #D4E697; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Mexican territory, 1848</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFFE0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> After treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1846, relations between the two countries had deteriorated considerably and on April 23, 1846, the president of Mexico issued a proclamation, declaring Mexico's intent to fight a "defensive war" against the encroachment of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker_2013_p.718_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2013_p.718-56">[56]</a></sup> On April 25, 1846, 2,000 Mexican cavalry crossed into the disputed territory and routed a small detachment of American soldiers sparking the "Thornton Affair" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker_2013_p.718_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2013_p.718-56">[56]</a></sup> Polk received word of the Thornton Affair, which, added to the Mexican government's rejection of Slidell, Polk believed, constituted a <i><a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">casus belli</a></i> (cause for war).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> His message to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> on May 11, 1846, claimed that "Mexico has passed the boundary of the United States, has invaded our territory and shed American blood upon American soil."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. Congress approved the declaration of war on May 13, 1846, after a few hours of debate, with southern Democrats in strong support. Sixty-seven Whigs voted against the war on a key slavery amendment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer68_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer68-60">[60]</a></sup> but on the final passage only 14 <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whigs</a> voted no,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer68_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer68-60">[60]</a></sup> including Rep. <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a>.</p>
<p>In Mexico, although <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Paredes_(President_of_Mexico)" title="Mariano Paredes (President of Mexico)">President Paredes</a> issued a manifesto on May 23, 1846 and a declaration of a defensive war on April 23, both of which are considered by some the de facto start of the war, Mexico officially declared war by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_Mexico" title="Congress of Mexico">Congress</a> on July 7, 1846.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antonio_L.C3.B3pez_de_Santa_Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Antonio López de Santa Anna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Once the U.S. declared war on Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> wrote to the Mexican government, saying he no longer had aspirations to the presidency, but would eagerly use his military experience to fight off the foreign invasion of Mexico as he had before. President <a href="/wiki/Valent%C3%ADn_G%C3%B3mez_Far%C3%ADas" title="Valentín Gómez Farías">Valentín Gómez Farías</a>, a civilian, was desperate enough to accept the offer and allowed Santa Anna to return. Meanwhile, Santa Anna had secretly been dealing with representatives of the U.S., pledging that if he were allowed back in Mexico through the U.S. naval blockades he would work to sell all contested territory to the United States at a reasonable price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Once back in Mexico at the head of an army, Santa Anna reneged on both agreements. He declared himself president once again and unsuccessfully tried to fight off the U.S. invasion.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction_in_the_United_States">Reaction in the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexican%E2%80%93American_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reaction in the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
